## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (position-dependent), damping (velocity-dependent), or driving (time-dependent).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing model)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (parametric excitation)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) ŌåÆ symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x┬▓) ŌåÆ asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Products of x┬▓ and v (x┬▓*v terms) ŌåÆ amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators like van der Pol
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) ŌåÆ external periodic driving force, expect resonance phenomena
- Cubic position terms with sign opposite to linear term ŌåÆ hardening (same sign as x┬│>0) or softening (opposite) spring behavior
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v┬│) ŌåÆ dissipative forces that respect time-reversal antisymmetry
- Product of position and time-periodic function x*cos(c*t) ŌåÆ parametric excitation leading to parametric resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence ŌåÆ autonomous system where energy is either conserved or monotonically changing
